  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText13440235754174882248" style="display:none">Sophie Foster thought she was safe. Settled into her home at Havenfield, surrounded by friends, and using her unique telepathic abilities to train Silveny--the first female alicorn ever seen in the Lost Cities--her life finally seems to be coming together. <br /><br />But Sophie's kidnappers are still out there. And when Sophie discovers new messages and clues from the mysterious Black Swan group, she’s forced to take a terrifying risk—one that puts everyone in incredible danger. <br /><br />As long buried secrets rise to the surface, it’s once again up to Sophie to uncover hidden memories—before someone close to her is lost forever. <br /><br />In this second book in the Keeper of the Lost Cities series, Sophie must journey to the darkest corners of her luminous world in a sequel that will leave you breathless for more.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it

I think I'm going to stick with it till the end.<br/><br/>Q:<br/>I think we could all use a little more weird in our lives. ( c) <br/>Q: <br/>It was a dangerous world for a sparkly flying horse. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>In fact, most of the great human innovations of the last few centuries happened under elvin tutelage. Electricity. Penicillin. Chocolate cake. (c)<br/>Q:<br/>“Each Wanderling’s seed is coiled with a single hair from the one who’s been lost,” he explained. “When it sprouts, </span>
  <span id="freeText16557554832491982732" style="display:none">Epic. Different. Capturing. Can't get enough of this series. I think I'm going to stick with it till the end.<br /><br />Q:<br />I think we could all use a little more weird in our lives. ( c) <br />Q: <br />It was a dangerous world for a sparkly flying horse. (c)<br />Q:<br />In fact, most of the great human innovations of the last few centuries happened under elvin tutelage. Electricity. Penicillin. Chocolate cake. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Each Wanderling’s seed is coiled with a single hair from the one who’s been lost,” he explained. “When it sprouts, it absorbs their DNA, taking on some of the attributes of the life they now share. Letting the lost live on.”<br />Those who wander are not lost . (c) Ok, this is a beautiful idea of expressing sorrow in a world where it's largely unknown.<br />Q:<br />Apparently, terrifying her only friend was better than snacks. (c)<br />Q:<br />Our long-lost elf, and the most searched-for creature on the planet, stumbling across each other in the middle of a forest in the Forbidden Cities. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Well, then why don’t you go visit him there? I’m sure Kesler would let him take a break. Or you could stay there and put your fabulous alchemy skills to use. Maybe you’ll be the one to finally burn down that ugly store.” (с)<br />Q:<br />It was a tiny thing, really. Just a small bit of encouragement.<br />But it meant something. <br />It meant everything. (c)<br />Q:<br />“School starts in a little more than a week?”<br />She’d known it was coming up, but that suddenly felt very, very soon. (c)<br />Q:<br />There were many, many questions racing through Sophie’s mind as she scratched her neck where the furry collar was tickling it. But the most important one was probably, “Why am I dressed like a shaggy elephant? (c)<br />Q:<br />This is our chance to show the older generations what we can do.”<br />“By dancing like elephants?” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I’m a few minutes late and I miss all the fun.”<br />“Don’t worry, I’m sure Stina will pick plenty more fights with me before the year is over,” (c)<br />Q:<br />Would it be right to kill them, simply because we planted them by mistake? (c)<br />Q:<br />“Only elves would call tunneling to the center of the earth ‘logical.’ ”<br />“And only a girl raised by humans would think otherwise.” (с)<br />Q:<br />Sophie gulped down the words like they were cold water in the scorching desert. … And for the first time in a few weeks, the future was feeling bright. (с)<br />Q:<br />“So I wagged my tail when I was supposed to flick it—what’s the big deal?” … <br />“The ‘big deal’ is that this was your chance to impress the faculty—and instead you’ve shown them you’re just as ridiculous as ever. When are you going to start taking your education seriously?” (c)<br />Q:<br />She hated the way he stared at her. Like any second he expected her to sprout an extra brain and use it to take over the world. (c)<br />Q:<br />Things weren’t so bad, really. How could they be when there was this cool rush racing through her, filling her with life and energy and lifting her higher . . .<br />“Whoa—what did you give me? (c)<br />Q:<br />Guilt is a treacherous thing. It creeps in slowly, breaking you down bit by bit. (c)<br />Q:<br />SOPHIE NEVER THOUGHT SHE’D WANT to be the creation of a band of murderers—but now she wished for it more than anything else she’d ever wished for. (c)<br />Q:<br />“I need to look around a room that Grady and Edaline don’t like me to go into, and since your job is to report everything I do—”<br />“That’s not my job,” Sandor interrupted. “If it were, I would’ve told them how you sneak out of bed to read by the light of the moon jars you keep in your desk.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Really? You don’t think I look like a rotten orange?”<br />“No, you do. But at least it almost matches your freaky eyes.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Mr. Sencen!” … “Would you like me to extend your detention?”<br />“Tempting. But I think I’ll pass.” (с)<br />Q:<br />And I’ve been thinking—”<br />“Oh good, at least one of us should.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I don’t see how that’s fair.”<br />“I didn’t say it was fair. You either agree or you’re out.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Your dad seems . . . intense.”<br />“That’s putting it mildly. Do you know we have an entire room at our house dedicated to the Wonder That Is Him? He’s covered the walls in portraits and awards and has a life-size statue of himself in the center—carved out of Lumenite, so it glows. …<br />“What about your mom?” ...<br />“She’s a perfect match for my dad.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Of course he’s wrong,” Keefe agreed. “If anyone’s malfunctioning, it’s him—I heard him try to laugh one time and he sounded like a freaked-out banshee.” (c)<br />Q:<br />It was hard to catch something that could rip an opening in the sky and vanish into it. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Just so you know, you’re pretty much my hero now. It takes serious talent to freak out the entire Council. I may need you to give me some pointers!” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Um, who doesn’t want to know more ways to annoy people?”<br />“Trust me, you already know them all.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I’ll do everything I can to guide you through this. But you’re going to have to fight hard.”<br />“I always do.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Maybe it was just her rushing high from mending things with Fitz and Biana, but she couldn’t help feeling like something really good was about to happen. She just had to trust, and try. (c)<br />Q:<br />“And why do we need your spectacle?” Bronte snapped. “We’re perfectly capable of making one on our own.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Sophie was afraid of many, many things.<br />But she wasn’t afraid of herself anymore.<br />She could do this.<br />She just had to trust. And be willing to take the first leap. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Am I interrupting something?”<br />“Yes, Sophie and I were having a pleasant conversation. So I’m sure this is your cue to ruin it.” (c)<br />Q:<br />But she’d already faced her deepest fears. How much worse could it be? (c)<br />Q:<br />SOPHIE SAT ALONE ON THE cold ground in a shadowy corner of the valley, watching the beams of light twist and spin above the snowcapped mountains. (c)</span>

<div id="review_696266082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696266082" />
    <a title="Gillian Berry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry"><img alt="Gillian Berry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354328337p2/13535966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696266082?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Berry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Berry" href="/user/show/13535966-gillian-berry">Gillian Berry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=but-i-am-the-chosen-one">but-i-am-the-chosen-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=speshul-snowflake-mary-sue">speshul-snowflake-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=love-triangles-are-pointy">love-triangles-are-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=bookish-boyfriends">bookish-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=slam-bang-ending">slam-bang-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=liked-this-more-than-i-should-have">liked-this-more-than-i-should-have</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=hardcopies-i-own">hardcopies-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13535966-gillian-berry?shelf=love-quadrangles-are-pointier">love-quadrangles-are-pointier</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696266082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11992901539921225992"><a href='http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/11/review-exile-by-shannon-messenger.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Originally posted at Writer of Wrongs</a><br/><br/>My review of book one, <a href='http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/08/review-keeper-of-lost-cities-by-shannon.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i>
</a>, aka a guided tour though my insanity with Legolas the elf<br/><br/>Legolas? Where are you, boyfriend? We can't do this without you.<br/><br/>
  
    <br/>
    
      
        <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384380569i/6861711.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
      
    
    <br/>
    
      There are elves in this book. It makes sense.
    
    <br/>
  
<br/><img height='213' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384380569i/6861712._SX540_.png' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>NO, handsome, we're here for the book. <i>Exile. </i>We return once more to the story of Sophie Foster, the magical thirteen-year-old elf with three boyfriends and four thousand </span>
  <span id="freeText11992901539921225992" style="display:none"><a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/11/review-exile-by-shannon-messenger.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted at Writer of Wrongs</a><br><br>My review of book one, <a href="http://gillianeberry.blogspot.com/2013/08/review-keeper-of-lost-cities-by-shannon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i>
</a>, aka a guided tour though my insanity with Legolas the elf<br><br>Legolas? Where are you, boyfriend? We can't do this without you.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384380569i/6861711.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      There are elves in this book. It makes sense.
    
    <br>
  
<br><img height="213" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384380569i/6861712._SX540_.png" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NO, handsome, we're here for the book. <i>Exile. </i>We return once more to the story of Sophie Foster, the magical thirteen-year-old elf with three boyfriends and four thousand super special abilities. By the end of this book, she will have four thousand and <i>twelve!</i> Still three boyfriends, though. This little girl is doing life right.<br><br>Seriously, this series stresses me out because <i>I don't know which ship will win</i>. Why do you have so many boyfriends, Sophie, you greedy little pre-pubescent? I would tell you to share, but jail bait elf boys are not exactly my type. I usually have a really good nose for sniffing out the Chosen Ship, but this is too much for me. (Keefe (Boyfriend #1). BE KEEFE. Please be Keefe? Team Keefe.) <br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img height="170" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384380569i/6861713._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      NO, LEGOLAS, THEY WILL PREVAIL. THEY MUST. SHUT UP.
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>So, <i>Exile</i> picks up a few weeks after the events of <i>Keeper</i>, in which Sophie and her BFF Dex (Boyfriend #2) were kidnapped by EVIL PEOPLE doing EVIL DEEDS. Most of this wretchedly overlong book focuses on Sophie coming to grasps with the fact that the whole elf world thought she was dead and now fears her, unraveling the mysteries of the EVIL DOERS and the mysterious society, the Black Swan, and starting her second year at Hogwarts Mozilla Firefox Foxfire Academy. Sophie also visits the enormously creepy Exile with Alden, the father of swoony Fitz (Boyfriend #3). I really liked Exile. It's this creeptastic underground prison full of criminals with BROKEN MINDS. Their minds have been broken. With MAGIC. That stuff, and watching Sophie try to navigate these dangerous, jagged minds that are like quicksand, was fascinating and quite cool.<br><br>This book still has moments of ridiculousness. There is a whole fleet of superfluous characters with silly names, an endless number of fart and poop jokes (a quarter of which are legitimately funny, because I am a child), and silly world-building. Let's not even discuss the time all the little elf children have to dress up like furry elephants and do a dance. I'm expunging it from the memory banks.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384380569ra/6861714.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Legolas! Don't make fun of the furry elephant children! Even YOU would look bad in that outfit.
    
    <br>
  
<br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384380569ra/6861715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Okay, no, you wouldn't.
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>The eye rolls, they happened. The groaning, it occurred. The threats of DNFing, they were made. And then this book did exactly what the first book did! IT WON ME OVER WITH ITS WICKED ELFCRAFT! Or, mostly, its Keefe-craft. He's by far the most engaging, funny, and even heartwarming character in the book. *builds a ship* *sets it upon the high seas* SAIL, BABY MIDDLE GRADE SHIP! SAIL!<br><br>The good stuff in this book just sneaks up on you. It's weird. Like, you suddenly become engrossed without realizing it.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img height="200" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384380569ra/6861716.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      "Sneaky like this? By sneaky, do you mean sexy?"
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>With you, I always mean sexy, Legolas.<br><br>Also, there's a pretty, shiny, friendly unicorn with wings and she's cute and yesss, animal sidekicks. of course, only SPECIAL SOPHIEFLAKE can tame her (PLUS KEEFE BECAUSE KEEFE RULES), but yayyy, pretty horse. <i>Exile</i> has an inglorious number of gloopy, soppy, saccharine scenes, but damn if my icy heart didn't thaw. This book has quite a lot of feels, which rescues it from the occasionally absurd world-building. Sophie suffers, and it hurts. (Also Keefe suffers and that REALLY HURTS BECAUSE KEEFE.) Okay, so she'll probably "end up" (she's thirteen, no need to marry her off) with Fitz, but whatever. There are totally feels between Keefe and Sophie. Let a creepy human adult reader dream.<br><br>Honestly. I don't know what's wrong with me. Silly book, I must have your sequel! I must captain my ship to shore! I must know the mysteries! Okay, no, I mostly want to sail my ship. That's okay, right? I start off these books going, "No, nooo, ugh noooo," and I finish them totally in love and eager for the next. <i>Bizarre</i>.<br><br> <img height="225" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384380569ra/6861717.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, fine. You win again, Legolas. You always do. Stop gloating.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384380569ra/6861718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11992901539921225992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2882274436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2882274436" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2882274436?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2882274436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13899892515238141556">This one takes all of the amazing set-up from the first one and catapults the series into a new level. I can tell this is the start of an amazing ride. This review will have <b>SPOILERS</b> for the first book...as it is the second book.<br/><br/><b>Character development:</b>★★★★★<br/><b>Plot:</b> ★★★★ 1/2<br/><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br/><b>World expansion:</b> ★★★★★<br/><br/>Alright, not going to lie, <b><i>Exile</i> suffers from the mild sophomore slump.</b> It's coming off of a dramatic series opener where its world was expanded exponentially for the main characters, and now we'v</span>
  <span id="freeText13899892515238141556" style="display:none">This one takes all of the amazing set-up from the first one and catapults the series into a new level. I can tell this is the start of an amazing ride. This review will have <b>SPOILERS</b> for the first book...as it is the second book.<br /><br /><b>Character development:</b>★★★★★<br /><b>Plot:</b> ★★★★ 1/2<br /><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br /><b>World expansion:</b> ★★★★★<br /><br />Alright, not going to lie, <b><i>Exile</i> suffers from the mild sophomore slump.</b> It's coming off of a dramatic series opener where its world was expanded exponentially for the main characters, and now we've got to make sense of the intrigue. <br /><br />When we left Sophie Foster, elf and telepath extraordinaire, she had just been kidnapped by some rogue elves intent on killing her. She'd been tortured, threatened, and then rescued by the Black Swan, a rebel organization that we thought were the bad guys but SIKE, they might be...the good guys? <br /><br />Given this altering perception of Sophie's relationship with the Black Swan and the torture inflicted on her by another hidden organization, <i>Exile</i> kicks off with Sophie in a relatively dark place. She's dealing with the PTSD of being captured, her guilt over her friend Dex's involvement, and the strangely intense headaches she has every time she attempts to light leap (travel through space via light beams) or use her abilities. <br /><br />I found <i>Exile</i> to be another 5 star read, but <b>it was a hard to get through the first 100 pages or so as Sophie was struggling so much with her headaches, inability to sleep/process her trauma, and the problems placed on her</b> by the adult rulers, the Council. BUT, proving once again that this series is a winner, <b>once more plot points began to unfold I found myself hooked once again</b> into the action. Sophie's explosive adventures in <i>Exile</i> are just as page-turning as ever, and <b>it ends with the perfect cliffhanger.</b><br /><br />Like I mentioned in my review for the first book, <b>this series pulls no punches</b> when it comes to its narrative. <b>It is aimed for a middle grade audience—and it keeps everything PG with this in mind—but it does tackle some serious topics</b> and involves quite a lot of intrigue. While I was able to spot several plot points coming, I found the writing and world-building to be so good that I didn't care that I knew the big reveals. I've already read book three...and may or may have already bought the rest of the books in this series. <br /><br /><b>They're that dang good.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13899892515238141556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624449044" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12546114407842806418"><i>"I think we could all use a little more weird in our lives."</i><br/><br/>I liked this book even more than the first one! Although I made the mistake of writing this review after I finished the third book and at the moment I'm more than halfway through the forth book, I'll try to keep my thoughts as coherent as possible and not spoil anything. <br/><br/>This has become and all time favourite series of mine and my love for this series only grows as I'm reading the sequels. It might actually be extremely close to number </span>
  <span id="freeText12546114407842806418" style="display:none"><i>"I think we could all use a little more weird in our lives."</i><br /><br />I liked this book even more than the first one! Although I made the mistake of writing this review after I finished the third book and at the moment I'm more than halfway through the forth book, I'll try to keep my thoughts as coherent as possible and not spoil anything. <br /><br />This has become and all time favourite series of mine and my love for this series only grows as I'm reading the sequels. It might actually be extremely close to number one! It is so good and so underrated, like why aren't more people reading it?! This should literally become the new Harry Potter! <br /><br />The plot of this book was engaging from page one. I read this five hundred page book in less than three days! There's also a lot of action and I had so many moments when I was cry laughing. <br /><br />I was so happy that we got more Keefe moments in this book, although I was hoping for more scenes with him since he is on the cover of this book, but nevermind that we get more and more of him as the series goes on. Keefe will forever be my favourite character in this series. There are so many layers to him and I am not even joking the relatioship between him and Sophie is one of the most precious thing I have ever encountered. <br /><br />I don't really have much else to say since my thoughts of this book keep connecting with the third one, but please if you love other series like Percy Jackson or Harry potter, read this one! I promise you it is worth it!</span>

  </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3650302403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3650302403" />
    <a title="Layla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109681904-layla"><img alt="Layla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602279778p2/109681904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3650302403?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla" href="/user/show/109681904-layla">Layla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442445963" href="/book/show/22429494-exile">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109681904-layla?shelf=re-read-2020">re-read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3650302403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16999516627262108784"><b>~5 stars~ <br/>(Re-read 11/19/20)</b><br/><br/>I 100% liked this one better than the first. <b>And I'm not just saying that because I spent way too much time gazing at the pretty alicorn and my favorite character on the cover, though this cover art is my favorite in the series I must say.</b> There were of course some very, very, very minor things I didn't like, but they are so minor that I am just going to overlook them, because this book was amazing. I was never bored and I loved it. Plus, no book is perfect, and somet</span>
  <span id="freeText16999516627262108784" style="display:none"><b>~5 stars~ <br>(Re-read 11/19/20)</b><br><br>I 100% liked this one better than the first. <b>And I'm not just saying that because I spent way too much time gazing at the pretty alicorn and my favorite character on the cover, though this cover art is my favorite in the series I must say.</b> There were of course some very, very, very minor things I didn't like, but they are so minor that I am just going to overlook them, because this book was amazing. I was never bored and I loved it. Plus, no book is perfect, and sometimes it's okay not to be a pessimist that nitpickes things that aren't even that important.<br><br>The minor things is all the blushing that happens. I'm just convinced that Shannon Messenger just really likes that word, but I don't. I get too much second hand embarrassment. But since that seems to be a general trend that I can't change, I will just have to live with it. The second thing is<b> Fitz</b> *shudders*. His downfall obviously starts in this book, but for a second there I forgot I disliked him but I was quickly reminded. I never saw the appeal with him. He doesn't really have a prominent personality and sometimes is just plain annoying, but I don't utterly hate him like a lot of the people in the fandom. <s>I just kind of wish he would disappear so that Sokeefe can finally happen.</s> <br><br>Unlike the first book, which was very much formulaic and underwhelming compared to the rest of the series (minus Flashback) this book felt more special. The first book, as much as I hate to admit it, might not have been enough to get me to continue the series if hypothetically I read it for the first time now instead of the youngling I once was. That's why I would greatly urge anyone that has any interest in this story to continue on. The story does start to drag a bit at the end of the series, but the middle books are superior.<br><br>Other things I liked was the Team Foster-Keefe (+ Sandor) content. I thought Grady being overprotective and his dad instincts kicking in was so funny and pure. I also liked how we were able to dive deeper into the mystery of the Black Swan, and since this is a re-read I am now noticing the foreshadowing which is so fun. And Dex, our sweet cinnamon roll, I can't believe he gets pushed aside as a side character the farther we get into the series. <br><br>Overall, I recommend obviously. This is the first book I have given a full 5 star rating in the last like 3 months, which is both saddening and shocking. I hope this becomes a steak of positive book opinions to come because I don't think I can handle reading another 1 or 2 star book smh (though they are always my favorite reviews to write hahaha). Anyways, you should definitely check this book out. <br><br><b>Here is my review for the first book:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3603773404?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities:</a>★★★★<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605848377i/30402183._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16999516627262108784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2956494366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2956494366" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2956494366?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2956494366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2152371163415668000">4.2/5 | This just in: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a> is a scam. Everything <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien' title='J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.R.R. Tolkien</a> told you was a lie (according to this book). Whole thing’s a ripoff, you see, of the resident Elflandia of this series.<br/><br/>This was very nearly a 5 star read! It was <b>so enjoyable!</b> Definitely has a 5 star cover.<br/><br/>Can I just mention…<br/><br/><i>“I’m guessing humans taught you the earth’s core was either a big pool of magma or a solid ball as hot as the sun.”</i><br/><br/>…really? Are you telling me my entire field of study is a <b>lie</b>? Gods this Elvin </span>
  <span id="freeText2152371163415668000" style="display:none">4.2/5 | This just in: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a> is a scam. Everything <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien" title="J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">J.R.R. Tolkien</a> told you was a lie (according to this book). Whole thing’s a ripoff, you see, of the resident Elflandia of this series.<br /><br />This was very nearly a 5 star read! It was <b>so enjoyable!</b> Definitely has a 5 star cover.<br /><br />Can I just mention…<br /><br /><i>“I’m guessing humans taught you the earth’s core was either a big pool of magma or a solid ball as hot as the sun.”</i><br /><br />…really? Are you telling me my entire field of study is a <b>lie</b>? Gods this Elvin righteousness irritates me sometimes.<br /><br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br />You know, for a book with Keefe on the cover, the story was sorely lacking Keefe. He was nowhere for most of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13260670.Exile__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___2_" title="Exile (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #2) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Exile</a> and then suddenly everywhere in the last 100 or so pages.<br /><br />Standard plot algorithm:<br />-Sophie does something magically impossible<br />-Everyone else basks in Sophie’s extraordinary magnificence<br />-Sophie collapses from the strain of said magical improbability<br />-Sophie is carried to the Healing Centre<br />-Everyone else cries their worries and woes over Sophie (except Keefe. He opts to take the piss out of her instead).<br /><b>And scene.</b> Over and over. It happened in Keeper of the Lost Cities and its continuing here. A very simplistic plot with slight variation this time round. Is it worth mentioning just how much I appreciated this slight variation?<br /><br />I didn’t care much about the opening until Keefe arrived and made everything better. Love that dude. Anyway, we have the introduction of Buckbeak—er, <i>Silveny</i>. Who is Silveny, you may ask? Well, she’s this mystical, sparkly Glitter Butt alicorn that’s perfectly perfect and is the perfect pet for perfectly perfect Sophie. Honestly, I didn’t give a shit about the bloody alicorn; after 200 pages I was crying for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5265998.Shannon_Messenger" title="Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shannon Messenger</a> to move ON! <br /><br />On to better things, there was casual exposition here referring to the last book that worked nicely. They were subtle recaps spread throughout the book for the purpose of being effective reminders and I thought this was very successful!<br /><br />I also really liked that the stakes were much higher here than in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12842828.Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities___1_" title="Keeper of the Lost Cities (Keeper of the Lost Cities, #1) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Keeper of the Lost Cities</a>. Not everything was all sunshine and perfect Elvin rainbows; things actually went wrong with catastrophic consequences and the issues were not resolved within the next few chapters. The characters actually had to WORK to fix things. The story was surprisingly tragic, if anything, and was just so raw with emotion and accomplished in conveying a range of strong feelings from different characters – particularly Sophie. The time at which I read the sad parts I was in a foul mood, seeking some lighthearted middle grade to cheer me right up, but obviously didn’t get it and consequently almost cried a few times. I was unbelievably relieved with how the plot resolved! I do hope that the stakes remain high so that I can experience the fear I felt, the scale of <i>emotions I felt</i>, in future books. In other words: I hope someone dies or something because what’s a fantasy novel without the looming risk of perishing? A book that makes you feel things is obviously doing something right! <br /><br /><i>“They meant it as a joke, but…”<br />Sophie felt the same way when people teased her about being an inflictor – even when they were just having fun.”</i><br /><br />This message. This hit home. It resonated with me on a personal level, being such an obscure, often overlooked problem that many people – people like me – really struggle with: jokes hurting you and you not being able to say anything about it <i>because it’s just a joke.</i> The fact that this was addressed makes me admire this series on a much deeper level. <br /><br />Oh the advantages of having a younger lead; allows for a larger range of psychological problems to be addressed.<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br />I can’t say I’m too big on Sophie being this all-powerful entity that dwarfs everyone else around her—adults and children alike—in terms of capability. <br /><br /><i>“Hey, I can’t be perfect at everything,” Sophie retorted with a smile.<br />“True enough.”</i><br /><br />Hmmmm—are you <b>SURE</b> about that? Could’ve fooled me. Like, how many powers is Sophie going to get? Book 2 and we’re up to, what, 5 times as many as everyone else? At this rate she’ll be looking at 15 powers by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32762917.Nightfall__Keeper_of_the_Lost_Cities__6_" title="Nightfall (Keeper of the Lost Cities #6) by Shannon Messenger" rel="nofollow noopener">Nightfall</a>!<br /><br />Okay, sure, but, Shannon—whatever you do—<b>PLEASE</b> do not make Sophie a Mesmer! That’s legit the only special snowflake attribute she DOESN’T possess yet!<br /><br /><i>“Fitz shook his head.</i> It always has to be you<i>."</i><br /><br /><b>THANK YOU, FITZ! SOMEONE SAID IT!</b><br /><br />I’m starting this new thing that I’ll put in every Keeper of the Lost Cities review from now on. I’m calling it my ‘List of Things Sophie Gets That No One Else Does Because She’s Special’:<br />Sophie gets to take elite classes, Sophie gets to study at the Silver Tower where typically only Sixth Year students learn, Sophie can harness this unheard of ‘brain push’ ability, Sophie is the only one to ever communicate with animals in Elvin history, Sophie gets three hot and talented guys pining after her, Sophie gets 4672846871 special powers – ya girl can fucking FLY, for Christ’s sake! <br /><br />See, this is a shame seeing as, otherwise, Sophie is a really sweet, caring and genuine girl. I really wish she wasn’t portrayed as such a Mary Sue. <br /><br />Onto other characters!<br /><br />Keefe was great. He had a wicked sense of humour that, while at times was very much cringeworthy, somehow always managed to be charming! Slowly, but surely, I’m beginning to witness more sides to his character that don’t necessarily defy his lackadaisical demeanor but rather <i>reinforces</i> it in clever and meaningful ways. I can’t wait to see more from him!<br /><br />Thank the Elvin Council that Fitz is <b>FINALLY</b> showing some character! Sure, he was a dick, but it was better than his previous cosmetic kindness! The dude’s fierce and isn’t afraid to speak his mind. His jealousy of Sophie was SO satisfying! He voiced his thoughts on how ridiculous it was how freaking flawless Sophie was! Everyone else commented on her remarkableness so seamlessly, so casually, as if it were <b>totally rational</b> to praise her constantly! He goes through a lot here and I can more than forgive his actions. I really hope he doesn’t revert to his archaic ways and continues to show some flaws and quirks instead.<br /><br />I truly like Grady and Alden—both of whom are brilliant and believable father figures that make (mostly) wise decisions and would do just about anything for their families. I wish I could love Edaline too but legit <b>all she does is cry</b>. As much as I like Grady, Edaline got the short end of the stick; the disconnect in characterisation is abundantly clear. <br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br />On the topic of Foster’s foster parents: <br /><br /><i>“Slowly, gently, she pulled them into the light.”</i><br /><br />The progression of Sophie’s relationship with Grady and Edaline makes me emotional because it’s just so beautiful! They all love each other so much and she completes them. Words can hardly describe.<br /><br />Similarly: <i>“The others could move on if they liked. She wasn’t giving up on him.”</i><br /><br />Another absolutely precious relationship and the source of much of my grief with this book. Sophie cares so bloody much for Alden and I really am not sure about how I should handle it.<br /><br /><i>“Grady rubbed his temples. “So… Keefe Sencen?”<br />“What about him?”<br />“What about Dex?”<br />“What </i>about<i> Dex?”<br />Grady held out his hands. “Never mind.”</i><br /><br />HaHAAA! You see, dear and oblivious parent-ish of Sophie’s, ‘tis a complicated matter. Also: <b>you’re missing a dude.</b><br /><br /><i>“Lame. I vote for The Unstoppable Team Keefe! Or Team Foster-Keefe if you’re one of those egomaniacs who needs your name in there.”</i><br /><br />ME TOO, KEEFE! These two may just be perfection. Their banter is super adorable at this point in time but what <i>really</i> draws me to this pairing is the sheer POTENTIAL! Whenever they interact, a million possibilities race through my head. <br /><br /><i>“Ooh, are we making Dex blush?” Marella asked as she grabbed the seat next to Dex. “That’s one of my favourite games.”<br />“Mine too,” Keefe said, snatching the seat on the other side of Sophie. “Though it’s also fun making Foster blush.”<br />Sophie felt her face get hot and he smirked at her.”</i><br /><br />Like, what human being with a heart could possibly resist moments like that?<br /><br />I’m honestly not really giving Fitz a fighting chance in this love triangle (yes, I said <b>triangle</b> because, let’s be real, Sophie will only ever consider Dex her best friend). I always did bomb at impartiality. <br /><br /><i>“Just like old times,” Fitz said sadly. “I used to sit right here, giving you a dose every hour, watching the bits of colour slowly return to your face and hoping you’d wake up.”</i><br /><br />In all fairness, that was really sweet. I suppose I could be willing to see this pairing unfold as well.<br /><br />My poor, lovely Keefe: your situation is horrible but your family is so damn fascinating! We’re only given little hints of his home life spread sporadically through the series and I am absolutely <i>STARVED</i> to know more about it! There are so many possibilities to this particular plot point/dynamic and it is delightfully mystifying. That is clever writing right there, Shannon, because I <b>NEED</b> THE WHOLE STORY.<br /><br />… …<br /><br />I have high hopes for the future of this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2152371163415668000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1674636867772644867" style="display:none">Hey, can this come out, like, NOW, please?... Because I want it. NOW. CAN. NOT. WAIT.<br /><br />READ:<br />Okay, so I literally JUST finished it. AND finished reading the Acknowledgements, of course, because I'm just one of THOSE people.<br />And...<br />O...M...G...<br />I've never wanted to avoid finishing a book this bad. EVER. I WAS CRYING FOR IT NOT TO END.<br />Usually my fangirling and *dies* suffices, but I can't even try for this review, considering even I CAN'T. Doesn't cover it.<br />I REALLY Can't. I just.<br />Okay... *Deep breath*<br />This book... One word... Keefe...<br />Can I haz him?!<br />I want my own personal Keefe to talk to. I can't even describe. In the first book, in those rare, wonderful moments he was in the book, I hung onto every word and swooned uncontrollably. But this book?<br />KEEFE WAS EVERYWHERE.<br />It was like a dream come true. Sighhh...<br />If he doesn't end up with Sophie I'm going to explode.<br />Sophie is exceptional in this book. Like seriously, she's fabulous. SO MANY trials and troubles and she handled them in ways I didn't even expect: I guess I underestimated Sophie Foster a bit.<br />Never again shall I!<br />Dex was... Well, I felt like every part he was in he was just getting in the way of team FOSTER-KEEFE love boat, but, you know...<br />AND FITZ.<br />WHAT THE.<br />He got on my nerves! I was always deciding between Keefe or Fitz for my 'team' (Because I don't SHIP the Dophie (Dex &amp; Sophie)), but this book decided it. I can completely understand his motives, and I still LOVE Fitz, but... Keefe is the only one.<br />Yep.<br />Yep.<br />The plot was intense. It was interesting and fast paces and everything I was hoping for. The characters relationships all became deeper, and the story grew into something MORE.<br />SO. <br />MUCH.<br />MORE.<br />Silveny is my favorite Alicorn, ever. Even though I've never read about or seen another one, but if I had, SHE'D still be my favorite, I'm sure. I totally have a miniature 'Glitter Butt' sitting on my shoulder, along with a mini Keefe.<br />AW. A MINI KEEFE. HOW CUTE WOULD THAT BE RIGHT?!<br />But really.<br />I loved this book.<br />I LOVE IT I LOVE IT I LOVE IT FOREVER. <br />I will now have to hide until the next book that comes out... Oh yeah, A YEAR FROM NOW.<br />Thanks, Shannon Messenger for writing too fantastical, brilliant books that make me extremely happy and then ruin my life when their over.<br />THANKS. <br />REALLY.<br />I will now sing Shannon Messengers theme song:<br />TROLOLOLOLOL<br />Because I think she just likes plotting all of the ways to make us suffer more.<br />CURSE YOU!<br />*Swishes cloak and vanishes*<br />Poof.<br />*That was the dramatic POOF of smoke. In case you couldn't tell.*</span>

        <a title="Lerizza Mae (books&amp;teacups)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lerizza Mae (books&amp;teacups)" href="/user/show/26981048-lerizza-mae-books-teacups">Lerizza Mae (books&amp;teacups)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2766421439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299133518449722858">This book is more angsty compared to the first one. Sophie is <i>broken</i> or <i>malfunctioned</i> because of a certain event that happened on the first book. Because of this, unfortunate events happened in her stead and, now, must find a way to fix herself to right the wrongs. And one other huge event is...she found a unicorn (or an alicorn)! A sparkly, though stinky unicorn that can somehow transmit messages directly to Sophie's mind, just like Fitz. I wonder why. Hmmmmm. Read the book to find out.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553954848ra/27290633.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The firs</span>
  <span id="freeText18299133518449722858" style="display:none">This book is more angsty compared to the first one. Sophie is <i>broken</i> or <i>malfunctioned</i> because of a certain event that happened on the first book. Because of this, unfortunate events happened in her stead and, now, must find a way to fix herself to right the wrongs. And one other huge event is...she found a unicorn (or an alicorn)! A sparkly, though stinky unicorn that can somehow transmit messages directly to Sophie's mind, just like Fitz. I wonder why. Hmmmmm. Read the book to find out.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553954848ra/27290633.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first book focused more on Sophie/Fitz and Sophie/Dex dynamics, while this book focused on Sophie/Keefe. And I was shocked! I loved their dynamics better compared to the other two. It may be because of Keefe's witty banter with Sophie, and he may joke a lot, but inside he deeply cares for his friends as shown much on this book and he said so himself. So Team Keefe, you better have a banquet prepared for your new member! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though this can be subjected to change. <span id="freeTextContainer12033247960881582900">Need I even say it? Exile was aMaZiNg! We got to know Keefe better, and I must admit, he's growing on me. In the previous book, I thought of him as a big egomaniac, but alas, I was wrong! Keefe is one of my favorite characters now. Another part I loved about this book was Silveny, I loved the alicorn character so much, Her strong will, and how much she cares about Sophie totally made her a new favorite.   <span id="freeText12033247960881582900" style="display:none">Need I even say it? Exile was aMaZiNg! We got to know Keefe better, and I must admit, he's growing on me.   <span id="freeText3143269940167493261" style="display:none">WOWOWOW!!! THIS RIPPED MY HEART OUT!!! <br /><br />Here are the stats... <br /><br />Romance- Crushes, hand-holding, hugging, blushing... Pretty much nothing in this area. <br /><br />Violence/Content- Magic is used; mentions of people going insane; someone important in the book almost dying; injuries; scene with a prison (lots of people are insane/their minds are broken), uses of elixirs/medicines to heal injuries, etc. <br /><br />I’ve only read 2 books out of this series, but it is by far my most favorite series EVER!!! I have become VERY attached to the characters... <br /><br />The writing style is beautiful. It drew me in immediately, and I didn’t want to put the book down. <br /><br />Sophie’s courage is amazing! She almost dies several times in each book... XD I love discovering her new abilities right alongside her. <br /><br />Silveny was introduced in this book! He needs to work on his jealousy issues, but he is a best friend anyone would adore. <br /><br />The plot twists were incredible, and kept me on the edge of my seat. <br /><br />I love how book 1 and 2 end on a happy note. Everything is right in the world. Then you read the preface and first chapter of the next upcoming book, and you need it. ASAP.<br /><br />Give this series a try! It is definitely worth the read;))) <br /><br />Still #Team Fitz:)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8548236105211387519">So I finished this book about a week ago and I have been trying to write this review ever since but have been having trouble trying to explain it's brilliance. I am a huge fan of Shannon Messenger's work and have recommended the first Keeper to EVERYONE I know (boys, girls, adults, kids, teens) I just think it's that amazing...Let the Sky Fall completely surprised me by how different it was and I also highly recommend everyone to read it. However, despite how excited I was to read Exile I was al</span>
  <span id="freeText8548236105211387519" style="display:none">So I finished this book about a week ago and I have been trying to write this review ever since but have been having trouble trying to explain it's brilliance. I am a huge fan of Shannon Messenger's work and have recommended the first Keeper to EVERYONE I know (boys, girls, adults, kids, teens) I just think it's that amazing...Let the Sky Fall completely surprised me by how different it was and I also highly recommend everyone to read it. However, despite how excited I was to read Exile I was also really worried most of the time the 2nd book in a series tends to be not as great as the first in my opinion. In most cases the 2nd book seems to be setting up for the next book. Exile is a great exception to that. From the moment I picked it up I was completely swept back into the Keeper world and Sophie's story. One of my favorite things about this series is the world that Messenger has created you never know what place, animal, or character she is going to introduce you to next. I want to keep this spoiler free but I was super excited to have Keefe play a bigger role in this book as I find his character absolutely hilarious. I also got introduced to one of my absolute favorite characters in this book (it's a new one and will remain unnamed but I will say it's adorable and brings lots of sparklyness to the Keeper world). I could absolutely ramble about my love for this book forever but I will sum it all up by saying I loved everything about it and (no big surprise here) am dying for the third book!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17179555560636007177">Look, when I pick up the <b>sequel</b> <i>immediately</i> after I finish <b>book 1</b>, then you can be damn <i>sure</i> that I've found a <b>new favorite</b> series. <3<br/><br/>Ahh this book was <b>amazing</b>, I can't even. What is this? Can it please continue? <3</span>
  <span id="freeText17179555560636007177" style="display:none">Look, when I pick up the <b>sequel</b> <i>immediately</i> after I finish <b>book 1</b>, then you can be damn <i>sure</i> that I've found a <b>new favorite</b> series. &lt;3<br /><br />Ahh this book was <b>amazing</b>, I can't even. My <i>poor</i> babies, they went though <i>so much</i>. <i>Ugh</i>, why can't we <b>hug</b> fictional characters? it's not fair!<br /><br />I can't believe that after this <i>monstrous</i> slump I've been battling most of the year I actually read an almost-600-page book in like a day!<br /><br />Who am I? What is this? Can it please continue? &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="17179555560636007177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1555512038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1555512038" />
    <a title="Dana Salman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman"><img alt="Dana Salman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454265334p2/2246621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1555512038?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Salman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Salman" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman">Dana Salman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2246621-dana-salman?shelf=regret-buying">regret-buying</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555512038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16525265790864354486">March 6:<br/>I haven't even read much of the second book yet, but I opened book 3 at random and found this on the first page I came to:<br/><p></p><blockquote>
  <i>"Stay calm" Kenric told her... "Whatever's happening you have the power within you to fix it."<br/>"How can you be so sure?"<br/>"Because I've seen the wonders you work, Sophie. You just have to believe."</i>
</blockquote><br/>I just... I can't. That cheesy line... I immediately had to close the book. Well, there goes a little bit more of the already tiny amount of hope I had that these books wou</span>
  <span id="freeText16525265790864354486" style="display:none">March 6:<br>I haven't even read much of the second book yet, but I opened book 3 at random and found this on the first page I came to:<br><p></p><blockquote>
  <i>"Stay calm" Kenric told her... "Whatever's happening you have the power within you to fix it."<br>"How can you be so sure?"<br>"Because I've seen the wonders you work, Sophie. You just have to believe."</i>
</blockquote><br>I just... I can't. That cheesy line... I immediately had to close the book. Well, there goes a little bit more of the already tiny amount of hope I had that these books would get better - apparently Sophie still has her life hack on and people are still telling her how amazing she is.<br><br><br>March 9:<br><p></p><blockquote>
  <i>"Where is this place?" she asked. "The center of the earth?"<br>"Exactly."<br>"You're serious?"<br>"I'm guessing humans taught you the earth's core was either a big pool of magma or a solid ball as hot as the sun."<br>..."Only elves would call tunneling to the center of the earth 'logical'."<br>"And only a girl raised by humans would think otherwise."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><i>Pffft!</i> Okay... This scene of an episode I watched of <i>Futurama</i> today was too perfect for how I felt when I read this passage the same day.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1457549586p8/1404278.jpg" width="400" height="839" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>March 13:<br>Well, finished it yesterday. I really was at the very least hoping to give it a two-star rating (and going by that pattern the third book might've actually ended up being decent), but... aside from just being entertaining the same way <i>Twilight</i> is so bad it's entertaining, I wasn't able to take away anything positive from this book. It didn't improve on anything from the first book except for it no longer being too obviously similar to <i>Harry Potter</i>. This series so far has just been a big amalgam of all the things I hate in a book series. And as promised in my status updates, I'll be breaking these things down into a (hopefully coherent) bullet-pointed list.<br><br><b>- Fluffy glitteryness.</b> This is a problem I also had with the first book and hadn't got around to addressing in detail, but it's still relevant here: <b>the atmosphere of this world is just too puke-inducingly tame and ideal.</b> It's a world where no crime of any kind happens (usually), where death is an almost unheard-of occurrence, where everyone is a vegetarian (including the animals), where (if you're an elf) you live a very long time without having to worry about looking your age so long as you don't mind pointy ears, you get a cool ability that you don't really have to use for anything other than your own amusement (and you would never <i>dream</i> of misusing your power of course, because you're an elf and you don't commit crimes), and you're set for life financially from birth. <i>This</i> was the setup of the world Sophie is introduced to in the first book, a world that by its very foundation already significantly decreases the intensity factor of the series. In the beginning, I was willing to at least <i>try</i> to ignore how much this perfect dreamland setting irked me while reading this second book because, well, it's the second book and it's too late to change anything. <i>But</i> I still couldn't stop myself from snorting every time a sentence popped up describing how <i>delicious</i> a certain food was, saying it tasted 'of marshmallows and chocolate and a hint of something fruity.'<br>I do realize that it is not <i>necessary</i> for a book to be dark and gritty, and that this is technically a middle-grade book series (though I don't see that as an excuse... I mean even <i>The Magic Tree House</i> series had a sense of danger sometimes), but this was clearly written as a fantasy adventure series; it has a villain (somehow) and an ultimate goal, ergo the <b>characters have to face trials and tribulations before the end.</b> And when you've got characters who are as well off as they are here, I feel like the trials they face ought to be dangerous enough to compensate.<br><b>But Messenger settled for the bare minimum of conflict and misery to pit on our protagonist: embarrassment.</b> As if this were a slice-of-life school story (*cough*like the first book). When characters aren't telling Sophie she's amazing or worrying about her safety or her feelings, they're making fun of her when she messes up her lessons or for her frequent trips to the doctor's or some such nonsense. <i>
  <blockquote>"I can't be perfect at everything."</blockquote>
</i> No, of course not. Only when it comes to your plot armor, the one that <b>resolves whatever legitimate danger or conflict there could possibly be.</b><br><br><b>- Melodrama.</b> This is going to tie in a bit with my first point, in that when Messenger isn't listing an entire spectrum of colors to describe things or coming up with names like AcheyBreak for all that medicine Elwin pours down Sophie's throat like lemonade, she's assuring the reader of how serious things actually are by <b>making the threshold for consequences incredibly low.</b> Meaning that characters never actually have to go through a lot to suffer. The biggest example of this would be 'guilt'; elves, it transpires, don't have the capacity to cope with guilt (which is why they don't commit murder). So when an elf does give in to guilt their state of mind literally shatters and they go insane - a full on disturbing type of insane that starkly contrasts with the otherwise glittery perfect world the elves inhabit. I feel like I should have liked this idea when it was introduced, given that I suppose it <i>does</i> (to some extent...) explain why the crime-rate among elves is low, but it just ended up making me laugh. The visit that Sophie and her foster parents pay to an elf who's succumbed to guilt was such a sudden shift in tone, so extreme an introduction, that it became comical to me.<br>Another example would be Sophie's constant visits to the doctor's. People tease her all the time about having a death wish, but it's not like her getting injured is ever subsequent to something risky she does - it's just because some things affect her more strongly. Like light. And when she does do something risky - after people tell her specifically not to - it ends up not affecting her that much at all.<br>No amount of pain that <i>any</i> character goes through felt earned. Messenger cheats her way out of having to do something too major by making the characters blow more minor things out of proportion. Like when something sad happens to one of the main characters, it didn't affect me in any way because, aside from the fact that I knew 100% that Sophie would be able to fix everything since that is literally what she was created for, other characters just kept tearing up about it. <i>Every</i> character. At the smallest provocation. In book 1 I'd grown to dislike Grady and Edaline for the same reason; I understand that they had lost their daughter and that no one else could empathize with them, but she'd been dead for 17 years already and their constant weeping for her got in the way of any real characterization for them.<i>
  <blockquote>"I must say you're handling this very bravely. Alden would be so proud."<br>Would he?<br>Or would he think she cared less than the others who kept falling apart?</blockquote>
</i> No Sophie, that's not how it works. Different people cope with grief in different ways. Having every character even remotely affiliated with a tragedy get all choked up and puffy eyed does not make me feel the sorrow more, it just makes me exasperated. The closest Messenger got to making me feel real sympathy towards a character was in this sentence:<i>
  <blockquote>He smoothed his hair and gave her a weak smile. "It's one day at a time."<blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote>
</i>You see, that's all that's needed. Aside from that answer he gave to Sophie's question of how he was coping, Alvar acted completely rationally and normally the rest of the time. <b>Less is more.</b> A character who is usually very cold and unfeeling trying to restrain an emotional outburst is a much more affecting scene than a character, who'd always get leaky-eyed at the mere mention of a lost friend or past mistake even before a tragedy, getting leaky-eyed again afterwards.<br><br><b>- Plot.</b> Or rather the lack thereof, at least for the first half of the book. I know the overarching plot of the entire series is supposed to be discovering Sophie's past and finding out more about the Black Swan and the people who kidnapped her, but it's hard to feel excited for any of that when a) we don't even know who the kidnappers are or what it is they're after, and b) the only member of the Black Swan we've seen so far is Mr. Forkle. Not to mention the fact that Sophie is not the one pushing the plot forward - she's just being led around by the Black Swan. And in regards to plot for this specific book... well I mean, there's a unicorn (sorry, alicorn) involved. And I guess this is a big deal as apparently this discovery will 'reset the timeline'. Except not once was it made clear what that even <i>meant</i>. <i>
  <blockquote>"But I don't think she wants to be here."<br>Grady sighed. "None of the animals want to be here at first, Sophie. That's part of their rehabilitation."<br>"Then why do we do it to them?"<br>"You of all people should know how dangerous it is for animals in the wild. Predators. Pollution. Not to mention what would happen to a creature like Silveny if she were ever spotted by humans... The only way we can guarantee a creature's protection is to move them to our Sanctuary - and once they're here they like it."</blockquote>
</i>I don't know about other readers, but <b>the sheer stupidity in elf logic frustrates me.</b> As far as I could gather from the first book, the reason the elves have the Sanctuary is that they believe every creature in the world has a purpose they're meant to fulfill. Okay... maybe I could get by that, ignoring natural selection for a minute. But if you believe every creature has a unique purpose, how do you suppose they're going to act on those purposes after you've completely institutionalized them? I mean they literally force dinosaurs into becoming vegetarians... And they're so worried about an alicorn surviving on her own when <i>clearly</i> she's managed to do just fine without them.<br>Don't even get me started on the non-science elves base their technology around. If Messenger had just decided to go the magic route - just state outright "this is magic!" - then I wouldn't question anything she comes up with. But the elves just keep giving bullshit answers to Sophie to explain the impossible things they do while at the same time not explaining anything. I mean exactly what am I supposed to take seriously when the same people who constantly talk about genetics and DNA tell me to throw everything I know about the logical and physical world (that <i>clearly exists here!</i>) and throw it out the window? Had the elf world been on an entirely different dimensional plane or reality or something I would buy their messed up physics, but they live on earth, with humans, who have <i>apparently</i> been perceiving the world and its laws entirely <i>wrong</i>, given that elves base <i>their</i> logic on laws that are completely contradictory.<br><br><b>- Sophie.</b> Just... Sophie. Everything has to come back to her. I get it, she's the main character, but as I've said in my book 1 review, there's absolutely nothing about her as a person besides her hax abilities that makes her worth following as a protagonist, and she hardly does anything to further the plot on her own - she's a reactive character. Even worse than that, <b>other characters seem only to be there to interact with her.</b> Although unlike in the previous book, where I was jonesing for someone to give her a good smack for her stupidity, Sophie hadn't really done anything as offensive here, I couldn't help noticing how shallow and self-centered she could be sometimes - and I realize now that that's not at all surprising given that every other character's role when they get any page time is to obsess over her! <b>These characters have no identity outside of their relation with Sophie.</b> Now in a limited third-person narrative like this, it's understandable that the only time we'd ever see other characters is when they are actually interacting with or being observed by the protagonist - but it's still important that we feel like these characters actually do something with their time, important things even (plot-wise), when they're <i>not</i> with the protagonist. And I don't know about other readers but it never felt like that for me here; here, characters don't move unless Sophie makes a move. And Sophie can't make a move until the Black Swan makes a move. I'd sooner read this series if it was from the POV of the Black Swan! But instead we're treated to chapter after chapter of people worrying about Sophie, people comforting Sophie, people teasing Sophie, reprimanding Sophie, hugging Sophie, crying with Sophie, offering to help Sophie, keeping things from Sophie, Sophie Sophie Sophie.<br>And what makes all of this even more infuriating is that Sophie is constantly trying to push away the other characters when they come to help her! I understand what Messenger is trying to achieve here; we're supposed to admire Sophie for always pushing her friends away so that they aren't put in danger when they're with her. But personally, I can't <i>stand</i> it when a protagonist does this. <b>Constantly trying to keep other, sometimes infinitely more interesting characters out of the actual plot in order to 'protect' them does not make me admire the main character, it makes me annoyed as hell.</b> A main character who trusts their friends and works together <i>with</i> them are much more favorable and admirable in my opinion. I understand wanting to keep people close to you away from danger; but characters like Sophie never seem to realize that (for all her amazing powers) they are absolutely helpless on their own and the danger would be lessened by a lot if they would just let the other characters take the stage with them.<br><br><br>-<b>And finally...</b><br>Just because I feel like nitpicking a little, here's a bunch of sentences that stood out to me as being the most painful examples (besides the ones I've already provided) of my earlier points - or that I just found plain stupid:<br><br><i>"We all think your talents are awesome."....<br>"I'd agree with you... but you're forgetting how remarkable Sophie is."</i><br>Oh my God yes, I get it already!<br><br><i>"He's not my father."<br>A father wouldn't refuse to help find her kidnappers.</i><br>Geez, Sophie, stop looking for every excuse to reject your foster parents. Obviously Grady has a backstory on why he refuses to help the Council.<br><br><i>"Sometimes it sounded like they were saying 'he's useless'."<br>"You're not useless, Dex."<br>"I was to them."</i><br>Wait, why the hell are you taking offense at your kidnappers calling you useless? You already knew they only wanted Sophie! "Oh man, I wasn't talented enough for them to use in their evil plans! I have such low self-esteem!"<br><br><i>If hearts could sink, Sophie's would have.</i><br>Huh...? Was this supposed to be your attempt at sounding original, Messenger? I guess a simple "Her heart sank" is too mainstream?<br><br><i>...which reminded her of a weeping willow - if weeping willows had red leaves and bloomed with thousands of purple flowers....<br>Brant pulled open the lid, pulled out a square purple puff that looked a bit like a colored marshmallow and took a bite. Pink juice dribbled down...</i><br>Yes yes I get it. Purple is your favorite color.<br><br><i>A delightful and dangerous adventure with complex characters and relationships you'll root for till the end of time.</i><br>To clarify, this was not a line in the book itself, just the blurb on the back. I added it because it struck me as hilariously ironic. The most ironic words being 'dangerous', 'complex characters', and 'relationships' (oh yes, like Fitz and Sophie, Keefe and Sophie, Dex and Sophie, Alden and Sophie, Sophie and her foster parents, and oh right Dame Alina and Alden - cause goodness knows <i>that</i> was important enough not to forget).<br><br><i>Siiiiggghhhh</i>. Well, that's over and done with. Now time to go through all that agony once again in book 3; the last, hooray! Unless of course Messenger manages to pull something that'll magically make that fourth book look irresistible. If not, then I can finally move on to something (hopefully!) better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16525265790864354486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
